I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Time_System_Timezone assigns wrong date to logs after midnight
## Bug Report

**Describe the bug**
When parsing logs that only contain time (`HH:MM:SS`) with no date component, using `Time_System_Timezone on` with a UTC+1/+2 timezone, the parser incorrectly assigns timestamps to the wrong date around midnight. Times just after midnight (00:00–02:00) are assigned to the previous day instead of the current one.

**To Reproduce**

**Input log:**
```
[23:58:00] [Server thread/INFO]: Before midnight
[23:59:00] [Server thread/INFO]: Just before
[00:00:00] [Server thread/INFO]: After midnight
[00:01:00] [Server thread/INFO]: Still wrong
[02:00:00] [Server thread/INFO]: Back to normal
```

**Parser configuration:**
```
[PARSER]
    Name        paper
    Format      regex
    Regex       ^\[(?<time>\d{2}:\d{2}:\d{2})\] \[(?<thread>[^/]+)/(?<level>\w+)\]: (?<message>.*)
    Time_Key    time
    Time_Format %H:%M:%S
    Time_System_Timezone on
```

**Steps:**
1. Create test log file with the input above
2. Configure Fluent Bit parser as shown
3. Set `TZ=Europe/Stockholm` in environment
4. Run and observe output timestamps

**Expected behavior**
Timestamps should be increasing and assigned to the correct date (March 30 in this case, not March 29).

**Actual behavior**
The 00:00 and 00:01 entries receive unix timestamps earlier than the 23:58 and 23:59 entries, indicating assignment to the previous day.

**Output example:**
```
[0] [[1774907880.000000000, ...], "Before midnight"]      # March 30, 23:58 - Correct
[1] [[1774907940.000000000, ...], "Just before"]          # March 30, 23:59 - Correct
[2] [[1774821600.000000000, ...], "After midnight"]       # March 29, 00:00 - Incorrect
[3] [[1774821660.000000000, ...], "Still wrong"]          # March 29, 00:01 - Incorrect
[4] [[1774828800.000000000, ...], "Back to normal"]       # March 30, 02:00 - Correct
```

**Your Environment**
* **Version used:** 4.2.3
* **Configuration:** Classic format (shown above)
* **Environment:** Docker container with `TZ=Europe/Stockholm`
* **Operating System:** macOS (Docker)
* **Timezone:** Europe/Stockholm (UTC+2, CEST)

**Additional context**
This affects parsing of logs that only contain time information without date. The bug becomes apparent when logs are parsed around the midnight boundary, making logs between 00:00–02:00 appear on the wrong date in downstream systems like OpenSearch.

</pr_description>

    47	static inline uint32_t digits10(uint64_t v) {
    48	    if (v < 10) return 1;
    49	    if (v < 100) return 2;
    50	    if (v < 1000) return 3;
    51	    if (v < 1000000000000UL) {
    52	        if (v < 100000000UL) {
    53	            if (v < 1000000) {
    54	                if (v < 10000) return 4;
    55	                return 5 + (v >= 100000);
    56	            }
    57	            return 7 + (v >= 10000000UL);
    58	        }
    59	        if (v < 10000000000UL) {
    60	            return 9 + (v >= 1000000000UL);
    61	        }
    62	        return 11 + (v >= 100000000000UL);
    63	    }
    64	    return 12 + digits10(v / 1000000000000UL);
    65	}
    66	
    67	static unsigned u64_to_str(uint64_t value, char* dst) {
    68	    static const char digits[201] =
    69	        "0001020304050607080910111213141516171819"
    70	        "2021222324252627282930313233343536373839"
    71	        "4041424344454647484950515253545556575859"
    72	        "6061626364656667686970717273747576777879"
    73	        "8081828384858687888990919293949596979899";
    74	    uint32_t const length = digits10(value);
    75	    uint32_t next = length - 1;
    76	    while (value >= 100) {
    77	        int const i = (value % 100) * 2;
    78	        value /= 100;
    79	        dst[next] = digits[i + 1];
    80	        dst[next - 1] = digits[i];
    81	        next -= 2;
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    /* Handle last 1-2 digits */
    85	    if (value < 10) {
    86	        dst[next] = '0' + (uint32_t) value;
    87	    } else {
    88	        int i = (uint32_t) value * 2;
    89	        dst[next] = digits[i + 1];
    90	        dst[next - 1] = digits[i];
    91	    }
    92	    return length;
    93	}

   115	/*
   116	 * This function is used to free all aspects of a parser
   117	 * which is provided by the caller of flb_create_parser.
   118	 * Specifically, this function frees all but parser.types and
   119	 * parser.decoders from a parser.
   120	 *
   121	 * This function is only to be used in parser creation routines.
   122	 */
   123	static void flb_interim_parser_destroy(struct flb_parser *parser)
   124	{
   125	    if (parser->type == FLB_PARSER_REGEX) {
   126	        flb_regex_destroy(parser->regex);
   127	        flb_free(parser->p_regex);
   128	    }
   129	
   130	    flb_free(parser->name);
   131	    if (parser->time_fmt) {
   132	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt);
   133	    }
   134	    if (parser->time_fmt_year) {
   135	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt_year);
   136	    }
   137	    if (parser->time_fmt_full) {
   138	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt_full);
   139	    }
   140	    if (parser->time_key) {
   141	        flb_free(parser->time_key);
   142	    }
   143	
   144	    mk_list_del(&parser->_head);
   145	    flb_free(parser);
   146	}
   147	
   148	struct flb_parser *flb_parser_create(const char *name, const char *format,
   149	                                     const char *p_regex,
   150	                                     int skip_empty,
   151	                                     const char *time_fmt, const char *time_key,
   152	                                     const char *time_offset,
   153	                                     int time_keep,
   154	                                     int time_strict,
   155	                                     int time_system_timezone,
   156	                                     int logfmt_no_bare_keys,
   157	                                     struct flb_parser_types *types,
   158	                                     int types_len,
   159	                                     struct mk_list *decoders,
   160	                                     struct flb_config *config)
   161	{
   162	    int ret;
   163	    int len;
   164	    int diff = 0;
   165	    int size;
   166	    int is_epoch = FLB_FALSE;
   167	    char *tmp;
   168	    char *timeptr;
   169	    struct mk_list *head;
   170	    struct flb_parser *p;
   171	    struct flb_regex *regex;
   172	
   173	    /* Iterate current parsers and make sure the new one don't exists */
   174	    mk_list_foreach(head, &config->parsers) {
   175	        p = mk_list_entry(head, struct flb_parser, _head);
   176	        if (p->name && strcmp(p->name, name) == 0) {
   177	            flb_error("[parser] parser named '%s' already exists, skip.",
   178	                      name);
   179	            return NULL;
   180	        }
   181	    }
   182	
   183	    /* Allocate context */
   184	    p = flb_calloc(1, sizeof(struct flb_parser));
   185	    if (!p) {
   186	        flb_errno();
   187	        return NULL;
   188	    }
   189	    p->decoders = decoders;
   190	    mk_list_add(&p->_head, &config->parsers);
   191	
   192	    /* Format lookup */
   193	    if (strcasecmp(format, "regex") == 0) {
   194	        p->type = FLB_PARSER_REGEX;
   195	    }
   196	    else if (strcasecmp(format, "json") == 0) {
   197	        p->type = FLB_PARSER_JSON;
   198	    }
   199	    else if (strcasecmp(format, "ltsv") == 0) {
   200	        p->type = FLB_PARSER_LTSV;
   201	    }
   202	    else if (strcasecmp(format, "logfmt") == 0) {
   203	        p->type = FLB_PARSER_LOGFMT;
   204	    }
   205	    else {
   206	        flb_error("[parser:%s] Invalid format %s", name, format);
   207	        mk_list_del(&p->_head);
   208	        flb_free(p);
   209	        return NULL;
   210	    }
   211	
   212	    if (p->type == FLB_PARSER_REGEX) {
   213	        if (!p_regex) {
   214	            flb_error("[parser:%s] Invalid regex pattern", name);
   215	            mk_list_del(&p->_head);
   216	            flb_free(p);
   217	            return NULL;
   218	        }
   219	
   220	        regex = flb_regex_create(p_regex);
   221	        if (!regex) {
   222	            flb_error("[parser:%s] Invalid regex pattern %s", name, p_regex);
   223	            mk_list_del(&p->_head);
   224	            flb_free(p);
   225	            return NULL;
   226	        }
   227	        p->regex = regex;
   228	        p->skip_empty = skip_empty;
   229	        p->p_regex = flb_strdup(p_regex);
   230	    }
   231	
   232	    p->name = flb_strdup(name);
   233	
   234	    if (time_fmt) {
   235	        p->time_fmt_full = flb_strdup(time_fmt);
   236	        if (!p->time_fmt_full) {
   237	            flb_error("[parser:%s] could not duplicate time fmt full", name);
   238	            flb_interim_parser_destroy(p);
   239	            return NULL;
   240	        }
   241	        p->time_fmt = flb_strdup(time_fmt);
   242	        if (!p->time_fmt) {
   243	            flb_error("[parser:%s] could not duplicate time fmt", name);
   244	            flb_interim_parser_destroy(p);
   245	            return NULL;
   246	        }
   247	
   248	        /* Check if the format is considering the year */
   249	        if (strstr(p->time_fmt, "%Y") || strstr(p->time_fmt, "%y")) {
   250	            p->time_with_year = FLB_TRUE;
   251	        }
   252	        else if (strstr(p->time_fmt, "%s")) {
   253	            is_epoch = FLB_TRUE;
   254	            p->time_with_year = FLB_TRUE;
   255	        }
   256	        else {
   257	            size = strlen(p->time_fmt);
   258	            p->time_with_year = FLB_FALSE;
   259	            p->time_fmt_year = flb_malloc(size + 4);
   260	            if (!p->time_fmt_year) {
   261	                flb_errno();
   262	                flb_interim_parser_destroy(p);
   263	                return NULL;
   264	            }
   265	
   266	            /* Append the year at the beginning */
   267	            tmp = p->time_fmt_year;
   268	            *tmp++ = '%';
   269	            *tmp++ = 'Y';
   270	            *tmp++ = ' ';
   271	
   272	            memcpy(tmp, p->time_fmt, size);
   273	            tmp += size;
   274	            *tmp++ = '\0';
   275	        }
   276	
   277	        /* Check if the format contains a timezone (%z) */
   278	        if (strstr(p->time_fmt, "%z") || strstr(p->time_fmt, "%Z") ||
   279	            strstr(p->time_fmt, "%SZ") || strstr(p->time_fmt, "%S.%LZ")) {
   280	#if defined(FLB_HAVE_GMTOFF) || !defined(FLB_HAVE_SYSTEM_STRPTIME)
   281	            p->time_with_tz = FLB_TRUE;
   282	#else
   283	            flb_error("[parser] timezone offset not supported");
   284	            flb_error("[parser] you cannot use %%z/%%Z on this platform");
   285	            flb_interim_parser_destroy(p);
   286	            return NULL;
   287	#endif
   288	        }
   289	
   290	        /*
   291	         * Check if the format expect fractional seconds
   292	         *
   293	         * Since strptime(3) does not support fractional seconds, this
   294	         * requires a workaround/hack in our parser. This is a known
   295	         * issue and addressed in different ways in other languages.
   296	         *
   297	         * The following links are a good reference:
   298	         *
   299	         * - http://stackoverflow.com/questions/7114690/how-to-parse-syslog-timestamp
   300	         * - http://code.activestate.com/lists/python-list/521885
   301	         */
   302	        if (is_epoch == FLB_TRUE || p->time_with_year == FLB_TRUE) {
   303	            timeptr = p->time_fmt;
   304	        }
   305	        else {
   306	            timeptr = p->time_fmt_year;
   307	        }
   308	
   309	        tmp = strstr(timeptr, "%L");
   310	        if (tmp) {
   311	            tmp[0] = '\0';
   312	            tmp[1] = '\0';
   313	            p->time_frac_secs = (tmp + 2);
   314	        }
   315	
   316	        /*
   317	         * Fall back to the system timezone
   318	         * if there is no zone parsed from the log.
   319	         */
   320	        p->time_system_timezone = time_system_timezone;
   321	
   322	        /*
   323	         * Optional fixed timezone offset, only applied if
   324	         * not falling back to system timezone.
   325	         */
   326	        if (!p->time_system_timezone && time_offset) {
   327	            diff = 0;
   328	            len = strlen(time_offset);
   329	            ret = flb_parser_tzone_offset(time_offset, len, &diff);
   330	            if (ret == -1) {
   331	                flb_interim_parser_destroy(p);
   332	                return NULL;
   333	            }
   334	            p->time_offset = diff;
   335	        }
   336	    }
   337	
   338	    if (time_key) {
   339	        p->time_key = flb_strdup(time_key);
   340	    }
   341	
   342	    p->time_keep = time_keep;
   343	    p->time_strict = time_strict;
   344	    p->logfmt_no_bare_keys = logfmt_no_bare_keys;
   345	    p->types = types;
   346	    p->types_len = types_len;
   347	    return p;
   348	}
   349	
   350	void flb_parser_destroy(struct flb_parser *parser)
   351	{
   352	    int i = 0;
   353	
   354	    if (parser->type == FLB_PARSER_REGEX) {
   355	        flb_regex_destroy(parser->regex);
   356	        flb_free(parser->p_regex);
   357	    }
   358	
   359	    flb_free(parser->name);
   360	    if (parser->time_fmt) {
   361	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt);
   362	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt_full);
   363	    }
   364	    if (parser->time_fmt_year) {
   365	        flb_free(parser->time_fmt_year);
   366	    }
   367	    if (parser->time_key) {
   368	        flb_free(parser->time_key);
   369	    }
   370	    if (parser->types_len != 0) {
   371	        for (i=0; i<parser->types_len; i++){
   372	            flb_free(parser->types[i].key);
   373	        }
   374	        flb_free(parser->types);
   375	    }
   376	
   377	    if (parser->decoders) {
   378	        flb_parser_decoder_list_destroy(parser->decoders);
   379	    }
   380	
   381	    mk_list_del(&parser->_head);
   382	    flb_free(parser);
   383	}
   384	
   385	void flb_parser_exit(struct flb_config *config)
   386	{
   387	    struct mk_list *tmp;
   388	    struct mk_list *head;
   389	    struct flb_parser *parser;
   390	
   391	    /* release 'parsers' */
   392	    mk_list_foreach_safe(head, tmp, &config->parsers) {
   393	        parser = mk_list_entry(head, struct flb_parser, _head);
   394	        flb_parser_destroy(parser);
   395	    }
   396	
   397	    /* release 'multiline parsers' */
   398	    flb_ml_exit(config);
   399	}
   400	
   401	static int proc_types_str(const char *types_str, struct flb_parser_types **types)
   402	{
   403	    int i = 0;
   404	    int types_num = 0;
   405	    char *type_str = NULL;
   406	    size_t len;
   407	    struct mk_list *split;
   408	    struct mk_list *head;
   409	    struct flb_split_entry *sentry;
   410	
   411	    split = flb_utils_split(types_str, ' ', 256);
   412	    types_num = mk_list_size(split);
   413	    *types = flb_malloc(sizeof(struct flb_parser_types) * types_num);
   414	
   415	    for(i=0; i<types_num; i++){
   416	        (*types)[i].key = NULL;
   417	        (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_STRING;
   418	    }
   419	    i = 0;
   420	    mk_list_foreach(head ,split) {
   421	        sentry = mk_list_entry(head, struct flb_split_entry ,_head);
   422	        type_str = strchr(sentry->value ,':');
   423	
   424	        if (type_str == NULL) {
   425	            i++;
   426	            continue;
   427	        }
   428	        len = type_str - sentry->value;
   429	        (*types)[i].key = flb_strndup(sentry->value, len);
   430	        (*types)[i].key_len = len;
   431	
   432	        type_str++;
   433	        if (!strcasecmp(type_str, "integer")) {
   434	            (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_INT;
   435	        }
   436	        else if(!strcasecmp(type_str, "bool")) {
   437	            (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_BOOL;
   438	        }
   439	        else if(!strcasecmp(type_str, "float")){
   440	            (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_FLOAT;
   441	        }
   442	        else if(!strcasecmp(type_str, "hex")){
   443	            (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_HEX;
   444	        }
   445	        else {
   446	            (*types)[i].type = FLB_PARSER_TYPE_STRING;
   447	        }
   448	        i++;
   449	    }
   450	    flb_utils_split_free(split);
   451	
   452	    return i;
   453	}
   454	
   455	static flb_sds_t get_parser_key(struct flb_config *config,
   456	                                struct flb_cf *cf, struct flb_cf_section *s,
   457	                                char *key)
   458	
   459	{
   460	    flb_sds_t tmp;
   461	    flb_sds_t val;
   462	
   463	    tmp = flb_cf_section_property_get_string(cf, s, key);
   464	    if (!tmp) {
   465	        return NULL;
   466	    }
   467	
   468	    val = flb_env_var_translate(config->env, tmp);
   469	    if (!val) {
   470	        flb_sds_destroy(tmp);
   471	        return NULL;
   472	    }
   473	
   474	    if (flb_sds_len(val) == 0) {
   475	        flb_sds_destroy(val);
   476	        flb_sds_destroy(tmp);
   477	        return NULL;
   478	    }
   479	
   480	    flb_sds_destroy(tmp);
   481	    return val;
   482	}
   483

    77	
    78	static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
    79	                                        int use_system_timezone)
    80	{
    81	    struct tm tmp;
    82	    time_t res;
    83	
    84	    tmp = src->tm;
    85	    if (use_system_timezone) {
    86	        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
    87	        res = mktime(&tmp);
    88	    } else {
    89	        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    90	    }
    91	    return res;
    92	}

  1159	int flb_parser_time_lookup(const char *time_str, size_t tsize,
  1160	                           time_t now,
  1161	                           struct flb_parser *parser,
  1162	                           struct flb_tm *tm, double *ns)
  1163	{
  1164	    int ret;
  1165	    time_t time_now;
  1166	    char *p = NULL;
  1167	    char *fmt;
  1168	    int time_len = tsize;
  1169	    const char *time_ptr = time_str;
  1170	    char tmp[64];
  1171	    struct tm tmy;
  1172	
  1173	    *ns = 0;
  1174	
  1175	    if (tsize > sizeof(tmp) - 1) {
  1176	        flb_error("[parser] time string length is too long");
  1177	        return -1;
  1178	    }
  1179	
  1180	    /*
  1181	     * Some records coming from old Syslog messages do not contain the
  1182	     * year, so it's required to ingest this information in the value
  1183	     * to be parsed.
  1184	     */
  1185	    if (parser->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
  1186	        /* Given time string is too long */
  1187	        if (time_len + 6 >= sizeof(tmp)) {
  1188	            return -1;
  1189	        }
  1190	
  1191	        /*
  1192	         * This is not the most elegant way but for now it let
  1193	         * get the work done.
  1194	         */
  1195	        if (now <= 0) {
  1196	            time_now = time(NULL);
  1197	        }
  1198	        else {
  1199	            time_now = now;
  1200	        }
  1201	
  1202	        gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
  1203	
  1204	        /* Make the timestamp default to today */
  1205	        tm->tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
  1206	        tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
  1207	
  1208	        uint64_t t = tmy.tm_year + 1900;
  1209	
  1210	        fmt = tmp;
  1211	        u64_to_str(t, fmt);
  1212	        fmt += 4;
  1213	        *fmt++ = ' ';
  1214	
  1215	        memcpy(fmt, time_ptr, time_len);
  1216	        fmt += time_len;
  1217	        *fmt++ = '\0';
  1218	
  1219	        time_ptr = tmp;
  1220	        time_len = strlen(tmp);
  1221	        p = flb_strptime(time_ptr, parser->time_fmt_year, tm);
  1222	    }
  1223	    else {
  1224	        /*
  1225	         * We must ensure string passed to flb_strptime is
  1226	         * null-terminated, which time_ptr is not guaranteed
  1227	         * to be. So we use tmp to hold our string.
  1228	         */
  1229	        if (time_len >= sizeof(tmp)) {
  1230	            return -1;
  1231	        }
  1232	        memcpy(tmp, time_ptr, time_len);
  1233	        tmp[time_len] = '\0';
  1234	        time_ptr = tmp;
  1235	        time_len = strlen(tmp);
  1236	
  1237	        p = flb_strptime(time_ptr, parser->time_fmt, tm);
  1238	    }
  1239	
  1240	    if (p == NULL) {
  1241	        if (parser->time_strict) {
  1242	            flb_error("[parser] cannot parse '%.*s'", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1243	            return -1;
  1244	        }
  1245	        flb_debug("[parser] non-exact match '%.*s'", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1246	        return 0;
  1247	    }
  1248	
  1249	    if (parser->time_frac_secs) {
  1250	        ret = parse_subseconds(p, time_len - (p - time_ptr), ns);
  1251	        if (ret < 0) {
  1252	            if (parser->time_strict) {
  1253	                flb_error("[parser] cannot parse %%L for '%.*s'", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1254	                return -1;
  1255	            }
  1256	            flb_debug("[parser] non-exact match on %%L '%.*s'", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1257	            return 0;
  1258	        }
  1259	        p += ret;
  1260	
  1261	        /* Parse the remaining part after %L */
  1262	        p = flb_strptime(p, parser->time_frac_secs, tm);
  1263	        if (p == NULL) {
  1264	            if (parser->time_strict) {
  1265	                flb_error("[parser] cannot parse '%.*s' after %%L", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1266	                return -1;
  1267	            }
  1268	            flb_debug("[parser] non-exact match after %%L '%.*s'", (int)tsize, time_str);
  1269	            return 0;
  1270	        }

2026-05-28 15:57:55,737 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I see the issue! Let me look at the `flb_parser_tm2time` function more closely and the callers:

The key issue is in how the time is parsed when there's no year in the time format (like `%H:%M:%S`). Let me trace the logic:

1. In `flb_parser_time_lookup` (line 1185-1221): When `time_with_year == FLB_FALSE`, it uses `gmtime_r` to get the current date (year, month, day) and prepends the year to the time string. Then it parses with `time_fmt_year` which is `%Y %H:%M:%S`.

2. The problem is that `gmtime_r` gives UTC time, but the parser should use system local time when `time_system_timezone` is set.

3. Then in `flb_parser_tm2time` (line 78-92): When `use_system_timezone` is true, it uses `mktime` which interprets the `tm` as local time.

The bug: When parsing time without a date component, the code uses `gmtime_r` to get the current date. But when `time_system_timezone` is on, the parsed time (like `00:00:00`) should be interpreted in the local timezone. The issue is that `gmtime_r` gives UTC-based date, but the time is then interpreted as local time via `mktime`. 

For example:
- Current UTC time: March 30, 22:00 UTC
- System timezone: Europe/Stockholm (UTC+2, so local time is March 31, 00:00)
- Log entry: `[00:00:00]` (parsed after midnight local time)

With `gmtime_r`, we get March 30 (UTC date). We prepend year "2025" and parse "2025 00:00:00" as March 30. Then `mktime` interprets March 30, 00:00:00 in local timezone (CEST = UTC+2), giving us March 29, 22:00 UTC. That's wrong - it should be March 31, 00:00 CEST = March 30, 22:00 UTC.

The fix should use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` when `time_system_timezone` is enabled.

Let me verify this by looking at how `flb_parser_tm2time` is called:



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && grep -rn "flb_parser_tm2time" --include="*.c" --include="*.h"

   170	void test_parser_time_lookup()
   171	{
   172	    int i;
   173	    int j;
   174	    int len;
   175	    int ret;
   176	    int toff;
   177	    int year_diff = 0;
   178	    double ns;
   179	    time_t now;
   180	    time_t epoch;
   181	    struct flb_parser *p;
   182	    struct flb_config *config;
   183	    struct time_check *t;
   184	    struct flb_tm tm;
   185	
   186	    config = flb_config_init();
   187	
   188	    load_json_parsers(config);
   189	
   190	    /* Iterate tests */
   191	    now = time(NULL);
   192	    for (i = 0; i < sizeof(time_entries) / sizeof(struct time_check); i++) {
   193	        t = &time_entries[i];
   194	        p = flb_parser_get(t->parser_name, config);
   195	        TEST_CHECK(p != NULL);
   196	
   197	        if (p == NULL) {
   198	            continue;
   199	        }
   200	
   201	        /* Alter time offset if set */
   202	        toff = 0;
   203	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   204	            toff = p->time_offset;
   205	            p->time_offset = t->utc_offset;
   206	        }
   207	
   208	        /* Adjust timestamp for parsers using no-year */
   209	        if (p->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
   210	            time_t time_test = t->epoch;
   211	            struct tm tm_now;
   212	            struct tm tm_test;
   213	
   214	            gmtime_r(&now, &tm_now);
   215	            gmtime_r(&time_test, &tm_test);
   216	
   217	            year_diff = 0;
   218	            for (j = tm_test.tm_year; j < tm_now.tm_year; j++) {
   219	                year_diff += year2sec(tm_test.tm_mon < 2 ? j : j + 1);
   220	            }
   221	        }
   222	        else {
   223	            year_diff = 0;
   224	        }
   225	
   226	        /* Lookup time */
   227	        len = strlen(t->time_string);
   228	        ret = flb_parser_time_lookup(t->time_string, len, now, p, &tm, &ns);
   229	        if(!(TEST_CHECK(ret == 0))) {
   230	            TEST_MSG("time lookup error: parser:'%s'  timestr:'%s'", t->parser_name, t->time_string);
   231	            continue;
   232	        }
   233	
   234	        epoch = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, FLB_FALSE);
   235	        epoch -= year_diff;
   236	        TEST_CHECK(t->epoch == epoch);
   237	        TEST_CHECK(t->frac_seconds == ns);
   238	
   239	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   240	            p->time_offset = toff;
   241	        }
   242	    }
   243	
   244	    flb_parser_exit(config);
   245	    flb_config_exit(config);
   246	}
   247	
   248	/* Do time lookup using the JSON parser backend*/
   249	void test_json_parser_time_lookup()
   250	{
   251	    int i;
   252	    int j;
   253	    int ret;
   254	    int len;
   255	    int toff;
   256	    int year_diff = 0;
   257	    time_t epoch;
   258	    long nsec;
   259	    char buf[512];
   260	    void *out_buf;
   261	    size_t out_size;
   262	    struct flb_time out_time;
   263	    struct flb_parser *p;
   264	    struct flb_config *config;
   265	    struct time_check *t;
   266	
   267	    config = flb_config_init();
   268	
   269	    /* Load parsers */
   270	    load_json_parsers(config);
   271	
   272	    for (i = 0; i < sizeof(time_entries) / sizeof(struct time_check); i++) {
   273	        t = &time_entries[i];
   274	        p = flb_parser_get(t->parser_name, config);
   275	        TEST_CHECK(p != NULL);
   276	
   277	        if (p == NULL) {
   278	            continue;
   279	        }
   280	
   281	        /* Alter time offset if set */
   282	        toff = 0;
   283	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   284	            toff = p->time_offset;
   285	            p->time_offset = t->utc_offset;
   286	        }
   287	
   288	        /* Adjust timestamp for parsers using no-year */
   289	        if (p->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
   290	            time_t time_now = time(NULL);
   291	            time_t time_test = t->epoch;
   292	            struct tm tm_now;
   293	            struct tm tm_test;
   294	
   295	            gmtime_r(&time_now, &tm_now);
   296	            gmtime_r(&time_test, &tm_test);
   297	
   298	            year_diff = 0;
   299	            for (j = tm_test.tm_year; j < tm_now.tm_year; j++) {
   300	                year_diff += year2sec(tm_test.tm_mon < 2 ? j : j + 1);
   301	            }
   302	        }
   303	        else {
   304	            year_diff = 0;
   305	        }
   306	
   307	        /* Compose the string */
   308	        len = snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf) - 1, JSON_FMT_01, t->time_string);
   309	
   310	        /* Invoke the JSON parser backend */
   311	        ret = flb_parser_json_do(p, buf, len, &out_buf, &out_size, &out_time);
   312	        TEST_CHECK(ret != -1);
   313	        TEST_CHECK(out_buf != NULL);
   314	
   315	        /* Check time */
   316	        epoch = t->epoch + year_diff;
   317	
   318	        TEST_CHECK(out_time.tm.tv_sec == epoch);
   319	        nsec = t->frac_seconds * 1000000000;
   320	        TEST_CHECK(out_time.tm.tv_nsec == nsec);
   321	
   322	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   323	            p->time_offset = toff;
   324	        }
   325	
   326	        flb_free(out_buf);
   327	    }
   328	
   329	    flb_parser_exit(config);
   330	    flb_config_exit(config);
   331	}
   332	
   333	/* Do time lookup using the Regex parser backend*/
   334	void test_regex_parser_time_lookup()
   335	{
   336	    int i;
   337	    int j;
   338	    int ret;
   339	    int len;
   340	    int toff;
   341	    int year_diff = 0;
   342	    time_t epoch;
   343	    long nsec;
   344	    char buf[512];
   345	    void *out_buf;
   346	    size_t out_size;
   347	    struct flb_time out_time;
   348	    struct flb_parser *p;
   349	    struct flb_config *config;
   350	    struct time_check *t;
   351	
   352	    config = flb_config_init();
   353	
   354	    /* Load parsers */
   355	    load_regex_parsers(config);
   356	
   357	    for (i = 0; i < sizeof(time_entries) / sizeof(struct time_check); i++) {
   358	        t = &time_entries[i];
   359	        p = flb_parser_get(t->parser_name, config);
   360	        TEST_CHECK(p != NULL);
   361	
   362	        if (p == NULL) {
   363	            continue;
   364	        }
   365	
   366	        /* Alter time offset if set */
   367	        toff = 0;
   368	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   369	            toff = p->time_offset;
   370	            p->time_offset = t->utc_offset;
   371	        }
   372	
   373	        /* Adjust timestamp for parsers using no-year */
   374	        if (p->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
   375	            time_t time_now = time(NULL);
   376	            time_t time_test = t->epoch;
   377	            struct tm tm_now;
   378	            struct tm tm_test;
   379	
   380	            gmtime_r(&time_now, &tm_now);
   381	            gmtime_r(&time_test, &tm_test);
   382	
   383	            year_diff = 0;
   384	            for (j = tm_test.tm_year; j < tm_now.tm_year; j++) {
   385	                year_diff += year2sec(tm_test.tm_mon < 2 ? j : j + 1);
   386	            }
   387	        }
   388	        else {
   389	            year_diff = 0;
   390	        }
   391	
   392	        /* Compose the string */
   393	        len = snprintf(buf, sizeof(buf) - 1, REGEX_FMT_01, t->time_string);
   394	
   395	        /* Invoke the JSON parser backend */
   396	        ret = flb_parser_regex_do(p, buf, len, &out_buf, &out_size, &out_time);
   397	        TEST_CHECK(ret != -1);
   398	        TEST_CHECK(out_buf != NULL);
   399	
   400	        /* Adjust time without year */
   401	        epoch = t->epoch + year_diff;
   402	
   403	        /* Check time */
   404	        TEST_CHECK(out_time.tm.tv_sec == epoch);
   405	        nsec = t->frac_seconds * 1000000000;
   406	        TEST_CHECK(out_time.tm.tv_nsec == nsec);
   407	
   408	        if (t->utc_offset != 0) {
   409	            p->time_offset = toff;
   410	        }
   411	
   412	        flb_free(out_buf);
   413	    }
   414	
   415	    flb_parser_exit(config);
   416	    flb_config_exit(config);
   417	}
   418	
   419	static char *get_msgpack_map_key(void *buf, size_t buf_size, char *key) {
   420	    int i;
   421	    size_t off = 0;
   422	    int key_size;
   423	    char *ptr = NULL;
   424	    msgpack_unpacked result;
   425	    msgpack_object map;
   426	    msgpack_object k;
   427	    msgpack_object v;
   428	
   429	    msgpack_unpacked_init(&result);
   430	    msgpack_unpack_next(&result, buf, buf_size, &off);
   431	
   432	    map = result.data;
   433	
   434	    if (map.type != MSGPACK_OBJECT_MAP) {
   435	        msgpack_unpacked_destroy(&result);
   436	        return NULL;
   437	    }
   438	
   439	    key_size = strlen(key);
   440	
   441	
   442	    /* printf("map_size: %d\n", map.via.map.size); */
   443	
   444	    for (i = 0; i < map.via.map.size; i++) {
   445	        k = map.via.map.ptr[i].key;
   446	        v = map.via.map.ptr[i].val;
   447	        if (k.type != MSGPACK_OBJECT_STR) {
   448	            continue;
   449	        }
   450	        /* printf("key(%.*s)(%d) == (%s)(%d)\n",  k.via.str.size, k.via.str.ptr, k.via.str.size, key, key_size); */
   451	        if (k.via.str.size == key_size && strncmp(key, (char *) k.via.str.ptr,  k.via.str.size) == 0) {
   452	            ptr =  flb_strndup(v.via.str.ptr, v.via.str.size);
   453	            break;
   454	        }
   455	    }
   456	
   457	    msgpack_unpacked_destroy(&result);
   458	
   459	    return ptr;
   460	}
   461	
   462	static int a_mysql_unquote_test(struct flb_parser *p, char *source, char *expected) {
   463	
   464	    int ret;
   465	    void *out_buf;
   466	    size_t out_size;
   467	    struct flb_time out_time;
   468	    char *val001;
   469	
   470	
   471	    ret = flb_parser_regex_do(p, source, strlen(source), &out_buf, &out_size, &out_time);
   472	
   473	    TEST_CHECK(ret != -1);
   474	    TEST_CHECK(out_buf != NULL);
   475	    if(ret < 0 || out_buf == NULL) return -1;
   476	
   477	    val001 = get_msgpack_map_key(out_buf, out_size, "key001");
   478	    if(!TEST_CHECK(val001 != NULL)) {
   479	        flb_free(out_buf);
   480	        return -1;
   481	    }
   482	
   483	    TEST_CHECK_(strcmp(val001,expected) == 0,  "source(%s) expected(%s) got(%s)", source, expected, val001);
   484	    flb_free(val001);
   485	    flb_free(out_buf);
   486	
   487	    return 1;
   488	}
   489

    44	static void cb_results(const char *name, const char *value,
    45	                       size_t vlen, void *data)
    46	{
    47	    int len;
    48	    int ret;
    49	    double frac = 0;
    50	    char *time_key;
    51	    char tmp[255];
    52	    struct regex_cb_ctx *pcb = data;
    53	    struct flb_parser *parser = pcb->parser;
    54	    struct flb_tm tm = {0};
    55	    (void) data;
    56	
    57	    if (vlen == 0 && parser->skip_empty) {
    58	        pcb->num_skipped++;
    59	        return;
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    len = strlen(name);
    63	
    64	    /* Check if there is a time lookup field */
    65	    if (parser->time_fmt) {
    66	        if (parser->time_key) {
    67	            time_key = parser->time_key;
    68	        }
    69	        else {
    70	            time_key = "time";
    71	        }
    72	
    73	        if (strcmp(name, time_key) == 0) {
    74	            /* Lookup time */
    75	            ret = flb_parser_time_lookup(value, vlen,
    76	                                         pcb->time_now, parser, &tm, &frac);
    77	            if (ret == -1) {
    78	                if (vlen > sizeof(tmp) - 1) {
    79	                    vlen = sizeof(tmp) - 1;
    80	                }
    81	                memcpy(tmp, value, vlen);
    82	                tmp[vlen] = '\0';
    83	                flb_warn("[parser:%s] invalid time format %s for '%s'",
    84	                         parser->name, parser->time_fmt_full, tmp);
    85	                pcb->num_skipped++;
    86	                return;
    87	            }
    88	
    89	            pcb->time_frac = frac;
    90	            pcb->time_lookup = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, parser->time_system_timezone);
    91	
    92	            if (parser->time_keep == FLB_FALSE) {
    93	                pcb->num_skipped++;
    94	                return;
    95	            }
    96	        }
    97	    }
    98	
    99	    if (parser->types_len != 0) {
   100	        flb_parser_typecast(name, len,
   101	                            value, vlen,
   102	                            pcb->pck,
   103	                            parser->types,
   104	                            parser->types_len);
   105	    }
   106	    else {
   107	        msgpack_pack_str(pcb->pck, len);
   108	        msgpack_pack_str_body(pcb->pck, name, len);
   109	        msgpack_pack_str(pcb->pck, vlen);
   110	        msgpack_pack_str_body(pcb->pck, value, vlen);
   111	    }
   112	}

   114	int flb_parser_regex_do(struct flb_parser *parser,
   115	                        const char *buf, size_t length,
   116	                        void **out_buf, size_t *out_size,
   117	                        struct flb_time *out_time)
   118	{
   119	    int ret;
   120	    int arr_size;
   121	    int last_byte;
   122	    ssize_t n;
   123	    size_t dec_out_size;
   124	    char *dec_out_buf;
   125	    char *tmp;
   126	    struct flb_regex_search result;
   127	    struct regex_cb_ctx pcb;
   128	    struct flb_time *t;
   129	    msgpack_sbuffer tmp_sbuf;
   130	    msgpack_packer tmp_pck;
   131	
   132	    n = flb_regex_do(parser->regex, buf, length, &result);
   133	    if (n <= 0) {
   134	        return -1;
   135	    }
   136	
   137	    /* Prepare new outgoing buffer */
   138	    msgpack_sbuffer_init(&tmp_sbuf);
   139	    msgpack_packer_init(&tmp_pck, &tmp_sbuf, msgpack_sbuffer_write);
   140	
   141	    /* Set a Map size with the exact number of matches returned by regex */
   142	    arr_size = n;
   143	    msgpack_pack_map(&tmp_pck, arr_size);
   144	
   145	    /* Callback context */
   146	    pcb.pck = &tmp_pck;
   147	    pcb.parser = parser;
   148	    pcb.num_skipped = 0;
   149	    pcb.time_lookup = 0;
   150	    pcb.time_frac = 0;
   151	    pcb.time_now = 0;
   152	
   153	    /* Iterate results and compose new buffer */
   154	    last_byte = flb_regex_parse(parser->regex, &result, cb_results, &pcb);
   155	    if (last_byte == -1) {
   156	        msgpack_sbuffer_destroy(&tmp_sbuf);
   157	        return -1;
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    /*
   161	     * There some special cases when the Parser have a 'time' handling
   162	     * requirement, meaning: lookup for this 'time' key and resolve the
   163	     * real date of the record. If so, the parser by default will
   164	     * keep the original 'time' key field found but in other scenarios
   165	     * it may ask to skip it.
   166	     *
   167	     * If a time lookup is specified and the parser ask to skip the record
   168	     * and the time key is found, we need to adjust the msgpack header
   169	     * map size, initially we set a size to include all keys found, but
   170	     * until now we just know we are not going to include it.
   171	     *
   172	     * In addition, keys without associated values are skipped too and we
   173	     * must take this into account in msgpack header map size adjustment.
   174	     *
   175	     * In order to avoid to create a new msgpack buffer and repack the
   176	     * map entries, we just position at the header byte and do the
   177	     * proper adjustment in our original buffer. Note that for cases
   178	     * where the map is large enough '<= 65535' or '> 65535' we have
   179	     * to use internal msgpack api functions since packing the bytes
   180	     * in Big-Endian is a requirement.
   181	     */
   182	     if (pcb.num_skipped > 0) {
   183	
   184	        arr_size = (n - pcb.num_skipped);
   185	
   186	        tmp = tmp_sbuf.data;
   187	        uint8_t h = tmp[0];
   188	        if (h >> 4 == 0x8) { /* 1000xxxx */
   189	            *tmp = (uint8_t) 0x8 << 4 | ((uint8_t) arr_size);
   190	        }
   191	        else if (h == 0xde) {
   192	            tmp++;
   193	            pack_uint16(tmp, arr_size);
   194	        }
   195	        else if (h == 0xdf) {
   196	            tmp++;
   197	            pack_uint32(tmp, arr_size);
   198	        }
   199	    }
   200	
   201	    /* Export results */
   202	    *out_buf = tmp_sbuf.data;
   203	    *out_size = tmp_sbuf.size;
   204	
   205	    t = out_time;
   206	    t->tm.tv_sec  = pcb.time_lookup;
   207	    t->tm.tv_nsec = (pcb.time_frac * 1000000000);
   208	
   209	    /* Check if some decoder was specified */
   210	    if (parser->decoders) {
   211	        ret = flb_parser_decoder_do(parser->decoders,
   212	                                    tmp_sbuf.data, tmp_sbuf.size,
   213	                                    &dec_out_buf, &dec_out_size);
   214	        if (ret == 0) {
   215	            *out_buf = dec_out_buf;
   216	            *out_size = dec_out_size;
   217	            msgpack_sbuffer_destroy(&tmp_sbuf);
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    /*
   222	     * The return the value >= 0, belongs to the LAST BYTE consumed by the
   223	     * regex engine. If the last byte is lower than string length, means
   224	     * there is more data to be processed (maybe it's a stream).
   225	     */
   226	    return last_byte;
   227	}
   228

2026-05-28 15:59:25,410 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I have a clear understanding of the bug. Let me trace through the logic step by step:

**The Bug:**

In `flb_parser_time_lookup` (line 1159-1278), when `time_with_year == FLB_FALSE` (i.e., the time format doesn't include year, like `%H:%M:%S`):

1. Line 1202: `gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);` — This gets the current UTC date (year, month, day).

2. Lines 1205-1206: `tm->tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon; tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;` — Sets the parsed time's date to the UTC date.

3. Lines 1208-1221: Prepend the year to the time string and parse with `flb_strptime`.

4. Then in `flb_parser_regex_do` (line 90): `pcb->time_lookup = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, parser->time_system_timezone);`

5. In `flb_parser_tm2time` (line 78-92): When `use_system_timezone` is true, it calls `mktime()` which interprets the `tm` as **local time**.

The problem: The date (year, month, day) is obtained from `gmtime_r` (UTC), but the time is then interpreted as local time via `mktime`. 

For example, in Europe/Stockholm (UTC+2):
- Current UTC time: 2025-03-30 22:00 UTC
- Current local time: 2025-03-31 00:00 CEST
- Log entry: `[00:00:00]` (local time, just after midnight)

The code:
1. `gmtime_r` gives us March 30 (year 2025, month 2, day 30) — this is the UTC date
2. The parsed time becomes: March 30, 2025 00:00:00 (in struct tm)
3. `mktime` interprets this as local time: March 30, 2025 00:00:00 CEST = March 29, 2025 22:00:00 UTC

But the correct answer should be: March 31, 2025 00:00:00 CEST = March 30, 2025 22:00:00 UTC

The fix: When `time_system_timezone` is enabled, we should use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` to get the current date, because the time will be interpreted as local time.

However, there's a subtlety: we need to look at how `flb_parser_time_lookup` is called. It receives `now` (time_t) and the parser. The function needs to know whether the time will be interpreted as local or UTC to set the correct date.

But wait, `flb_parser_time_lookup` doesn't have access to the `parser`'s `time_system_timezone` flag... Actually it does! `parser` is passed as a parameter. Let me check again:

```c
int flb_parser_time_lookup(const char *time_str, size_t tsize,
                           time_t now,
                           struct flb_parser *parser,
                           struct flb_tm *tm, double *ns)
```

Yes, `parser` is passed! So we can check `parser->time_system_timezone` inside `flb_parser_time_lookup`.

The fix should be:

In `flb_parser_time_lookup`, line 1202, change from `gmtime_r` to `localtime_r` when `parser->time_system_timezone` is true.

Let me also check if there are other places where similar issues might occur. Let me look at how the time offset is applied:

Line 1273-1275:
```c
if (parser->time_with_tz == FLB_FALSE) {
    flb_tm_gmtoff(tm) = parser->time_offset;
}
```

When `time_with_tz` is false (no timezone in the parsed string) and `time_system_timezone` is false but `time_offset` is set, the offset is applied. But when `time_system_timezone` is true, `flb_parser_tm2time` uses `mktime` which handles the timezone. However, the `gmtoff` might interfere. Let me check `flb_parser_tm2time` again:

```c
static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
                                        int use_system_timezone)
{
    struct tm tmp;
    time_t res;

    tmp = src->tm;
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
        res = mktime(&tmp);
    } else {
        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    }
    return res;
}
```

When `use_system_timezone` is true, it uses `mktime` and ignores `gmtoff`. So the `gmtoff` doesn't matter in that path. Good.

Now, the fix: In `flb_parser_time_lookup`, when `parser->time_system_timezone` is true, we should use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` to determine the current date.

Let me write a script to reproduce the bug first.

           tmy.tm_year + 1900, tmy.tm_mon + 1, tmy.tm_mday,
           tmy.tm_hour, tmy.tm_min, tmy.tm_sec);
    
    /* Now show what happens with "23:59:00" */
    memset(&parsed_tm, 0, sizeof(parsed_tm));
    parsed_tm.tm_year = 2025 - 1900;
    parsed_tm.tm_mon = 2;   /* March */
    parsed_tm.tm_mday = 30;  /* gmtime_r date */
    parsed_tm.tm_hour = 23;
    parsed_tm.tm_min = 59;
    parsed_tm.tm_sec = 0;
    parsed_tm.tm_isdst = -1;
    
    result = mktime(&parsed_tm);
    printf("\n'23:59:00' with gmtime_r date (March 30):\n");
    printf("  mktime result: %ld\n", result);
    printf("  localtime of result: ");
    localtime_r(&result, &tmy);
    printf("%04d-%02d-%02d %02d:%02d:%02d\n",
           tmy.tm_year + 1900, tmy.tm_mon + 1, tmy.tm_mday,
           tmy.tm_hour, tmy.tm_min, tmy.tm_sec);
    
    return 0;
}

This confirms the bug. Let me analyze the output:

When current time is 2025-03-30 21:00 UTC (23:00 local CEST):
- `gmtime_r` gives March 30, `localtime_r` gives March 30 (both same date in this case since 21:00 UTC = 23:00 CEST, same day)

But with the `00:00:00` parse:
- Using gmtime_r date (March 30): mktime gives 1743289200 = March 29, 23:00 UTC. This is March 30, 00:00 CEST — which is actually correct... but wait, it's not the same day as the other timestamps.

Let me re-examine. The issue in the PR is about times crossing midnight. Let me use the actual timestamps from the PR description.

From the PR:
- March 30, 23:58 - Correct (1774907880)
- March 30, 23:59 - Correct (1774907940)
- March 29, 00:00 - Incorrect (1774821600) - should be March 30, 00:00
- March 29, 00:01 - Incorrect (1774821660) - should be March 30, 00:01
- March 30, 02:00 - Correct (1774828800)

Let me verify: the issue is that when parsing times after midnight (00:00–02:00), the date assigned is the previous day.

My test above actually shows the correct behavior for `00:00:00` with `gmtime_r` when local time is 23:00 on the same day. But the problem occurs when local time has crossed midnight but UTC hasn't.

Let me test with a time where it's past midnight local time but not UTC:

#include <stdio.h>
#include <time.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

int main() {
    time_t now;
    struct tm tmy;
    struct tm parsed_tm;
    time_t result;
    
    /* Set timezone to Europe/Stockholm */
    setenv("TZ", "Europe/Stockholm", 1);
    tzset();
    
    /* Simulate current time: March 30, 2025 22:30:00 UTC */
    /* In Stockholm (CEST, UTC+2), this is March 31, 2025 00:30:00 */
    struct tm base = {0};
    base.tm_year = 2025 - 1900;
    base.tm_mon = 2;  /* March */
    base.tm_mday = 30;
    base.tm_hour = 22;
    base.tm_min = 30;
    base.tm_sec = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);  /* UTC */
    
    printf("Current time_t: %ld\n", now);
    
    printf("\n--- Current time breakdown ---\n");
    gmtime_r(&now, &tmy);
    printf("gmtime_r:    %04d-%02d-%02d %02d:%02d:%02d UTC\n",

So in the PR example:
- 23:58 → 2026-03-30 21:58 UTC = March 30, 23:58 CEST (correct)
- 23:59 → 2026-03-30 21:59 UTC = March 30, 23:59 CEST (correct)
- 00:00 → 2026-03-29 22:00 UTC = March 29, 23:00 CET? No wait...

But the expected date is March 30... so actually the epoch 1774821600 corresponds to March 30, 00:00 CEST. That seems correct for the 00:00 entry!

Wait, but the PR says this is incorrect and assigned to "March 29". Let me re-read:

```
[2] [[1774821600.000000000, ...], "After midnight"]       # March 29, 00:00 - Incorrect
```

The PR says the epoch is 1774821600 which is March 29, 22:00 UTC. In Stockholm (CEST, UTC+2), that's March 30, 00:00. So the local time is correct (March 30, 00:00), but the PR author is complaining that it's "March 29" — maybe they're looking at the UTC representation?

Actually, looking at it more carefully, the issue is about the date assignment relative to the other entries. The 23:58 entry has epoch 1774907880 (March 30, 21:58 UTC = March 30, 23:58 CEST), and the 00:00 entry has epoch 1774821600 (March 29, 22:00 UTC = March 30, 00:00 CEST). 

So both entries are on March 30 local time, but the epoch for 00:00 is EARLIER than the epoch for 23:58. That means if you sort by epoch, 00:00 comes before 23:58, which is wrong chronologically — 00:00 should be AFTER 23:58 (it's the next day).

The issue is that the date assigned to 00:00 is March 30 (from `gmtime_r`), giving March 30, 00:00 CEST = March 29, 22:00 UTC. But the 23:58 entry is also March 30, giving March 30, 23:58 CEST = March 30, 21:58 UTC. The 23:58 epoch is larger than the 00:00 epoch, which is wrong.

The correct assignment would be: 00:00 should be on March 31 (the next day, since local time has crossed midnight). March 31, 00:00 CEST = March 30, 22:00 UTC, which would give an epoch > the 23:58 entry.

So the fix is: when `time_system_timezone` is enabled, we should use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` to determine the current date. But we also need to handle the case where the parsed time is earlier than the current local time — in that case, it might still be on the same local date.

Wait, but that's exactly what `localtime_r` does! Let me re-check my test:

With local time March 31, 00:30:
- `localtime_r` gives March 31
- Parsing "23:58" with March 31 date → March 31, 23:58 CEST (WRONG, should be March 30)

But actually, when would you have a log line with "23:58" when the current local time is 00:30? In normal log processing, you process logs as they arrive. If it's 00:30 local time and you get a log with "23:58", that log is from the previous day.

However, the PR description says these logs are from a file being processed. The file has entries from before and after midnight. The processing happens at some point after all these entries were written.

The real question is: what heuristic should be used to determine the correct date for a time-only log entry?

Let me look at how the current code works more carefully and what the expected behavior is. The key function is in `flb_parser_time_lookup`:

```c
if (parser->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
    ...
    if (now <= 0) {
        time_now = time(NULL);
    } else {
        time_now = now;
    }
    gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
    /* Make the timestamp default to today */
    tm->tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
    tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
    ...
}
```

The `now` parameter is the current time. It's passed from the caller. In `flb_parser_regex_do`, `pcb.time_now = 0;` so `now` is 0, meaning `time(NULL)` is used.

The problem: `gmtime_r` gives UTC date. When `time_system_timezone` is on, `mktime` interprets the result as local time. This mismatch causes the date to be off by one when UTC and local dates differ.

But here's the subtlety: the date should be determined from the local time, not UTC, because the parsed time will be interpreted as local time by `mktime`.

Let me think about this more carefully. The fix should be:

When `parser->time_system_timezone` is true:
- Use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` to get the current date

This ensures that the date assigned to the parsed time is consistent with the timezone that will be used by `mktime`.

But wait, my test showed that with `localtime_r`, "23:58" gets assigned to March 31 (tomorrow) when current local time is March 31 00:30. That's wrong because 23:58 is clearly from the previous day.

However, in the PR's scenario, the logs are all from the same file. The processing happens after the fact. The current time (when processing) might be March 31 00:30, but the log entries at 23:58, 23:59, 00:00, 00:01, 02:00 are all from the "same logging session" that started on March 30.

This is fundamentally a heuristic problem. There's no perfect solution for time-only logs. But the current behavior is clearly buggy: the epochs are non-monotonic (00:00 has a smaller epoch than 23:58).

Let me look at how other tools handle this. The typical approach is:
1. Use the current local date

Actually, both have issues. Let me think about what the correct approach should be...

I think the real solution is more nuanced. The problem is fundamentally about the mismatch between UTC date (used for date assignment) and local time (used for interpretation via `mktime`).

Let me look at what happens when `time_system_timezone` is OFF (the default). In that case:
- `gmtime_r` gives UTC date
- `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=false` uses `timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src)` where `gmtoff` is set to `parser->time_offset` (which is 0 by default)
- So the time is interpreted as UTC

This is consistent: UTC date + UTC interpretation = correct.

When `time_system_timezone` is ON:
- `gmtime_r` gives UTC date
- `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` uses `mktime()` which interprets as local time
- This is inconsistent: UTC date + local interpretation = bug

The fix: when `time_system_timezone` is ON, use `localtime_r` to get the LOCAL date, which is consistent with local interpretation via `mktime`.

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/repro.c << 'EOF'
#include <stdio.h>
#include <time.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

/* Simulate the exact logic from flb_parser_time_lookup and flb_parser_tm2time */

/* from flb_parser.h */
struct flb_tm {
    struct tm tm;
    long int tm_gmtoff;
};

#define flb_tm_gmtoff(x) (x)->tm_gmtoff

static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
                                        int use_system_timezone)
{
    struct tm tmp;
    time_t res;

    tmp = src->tm;
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
        res = mktime(&tmp);
    } else {
        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    }
    return res;
}

int main() {
    time_t now;
    struct tm tmy;
    struct flb_tm tm;
    time_t result;
    int use_system_timezone = 1;  /* Time_System_Timezone on */
    
    /* Set timezone to Europe/Stockholm */
    setenv("TZ", "Europe/Stockholm", 1);
    tzset();
    
    printf("Timezone: %s\n", getenv("TZ"));
    printf("DST: %d\n", daylight);
    
    /* Simulate current time: March 30, 2026 around 22:00 UTC */
    /* This is when the log file is being processed */
    struct tm base_utc = {0};
    base_utc.tm_year = 2026 - 1900;
    base_utc.tm_mon = 2;  /* March */
    base_utc.tm_mday = 30;
    base_utc.tm_hour = 22;
    base_utc.tm_min = 0;
    base_utc.tm_sec = 0;
    now = timegm(&base_utc);
    
    printf("\nNow (UTC): %s", asctime(gmtime(&now)));
    printf("Now (local): %s", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    /* Test parsing times */
    const char *test_times[] = {"23:58:00", "23:59:00", "00:00:00", "00:01:00", "02:00:00"};
    int num_tests = sizeof(test_times) / sizeof(test_times[0]);
    
    printf("\n--- Using gmtime_r (OLD/current code) ---\n");
    for (int i = 0; i < num_tests; i++) {
        memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
        
        /* This is what flb_parser_time_lookup does: */
        gmtime_r(&now, &tmy);
        tm.tm.tm_year = tmy.tm_year;
        tm.tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
        tm.tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
        
        /* Parse the time */
        int hour, min, sec;
        sscanf(test_times[i], "%d:%d:%d", &hour, &min, &sec);
        tm.tm.tm_hour = hour;
        tm.tm.tm_min = min;
        tm.tm.tm_sec = sec;
        
        result = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, use_system_timezone);
        printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (UTC: %s", test_times[i], result, asctime(gmtime(&result)));
        printf("    local: %s", asctime(localtime(&result)));
    }
    
    printf("\n--- Using localtime_r (NEW/proposed fix) ---\n");
    for (int i = 0; i < num_tests; i++) {
        memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
        
        /* Proposed: use localtime_r when time_system_timezone is on */
        localtime_r(&now, &tmy);
        tm.tm.tm_year = tmy.tm_year;
        tm.tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
        tm.tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
        
        int hour, min, sec;
        sscanf(test_times[i], "%d:%d:%d", &hour, &min, &sec);
        tm.tm.tm_hour = hour;
        tm.tm.tm_min = min;
        tm.tm.tm_sec = sec;
        
        result = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, use_system_timezone);
        printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (UTC: %s", test_times[i], result, asctime(gmtime(&result)));
        printf("    local: %s", asctime(localtime(&result)));
    }
    
    return 0;
}

Now I can clearly see the issue:

**Current code (gmtime_r):**
- Now is March 30, 22:00 UTC = March 31, 00:00 local
- 23:58 → epoch=1774907880 (March 30, 23:58 local) ✓
- 00:00 → epoch=1774821600 (March 30, 00:00 local) but this is BEFORE 23:58! ✗
- 02:00 → epoch=1774828800 (March 30, 02:00 local) but this is also BEFORE 23:58! ✗

**Proposed fix (localtime_r):**
- Now is March 30, 22:00 UTC = March 31, 00:00 local
- 23:58 → epoch=1774994280 (March 31, 23:58 local) — this is the NEXT day, wrong! ✗
- 00:00 → epoch=1774908000 (March 31, 00:00 local) ✓
- 02:00 → epoch=1774915200 (March 31, 02:00 local) ✓

So neither approach is completely correct. The localtime_r approach gives the wrong date for times that are "before" the current local time (23:58 when it's already 00:00 next day).

But wait, in the PR scenario, the expected date for ALL entries is March 30. The current time is presumably March 30 ~22:00 UTC. But the PR output shows processing happening when local time is already March 31 (00:00+). If processing happened at March 30, 23:58 local (March 30, 21:58 UTC), then both `gmtime_r` and `localtime_r` would give March 30, and everything would work correctly.

The issue is that when processing happens after midnight local time, `gmtime_r` still returns the previous day's date, causing the non-monotonic timestamps.

I think the correct fix is: use `localtime_r` instead of `gmtime_r` when `time_system_timezone` is true. This ensures the date is consistent with the timezone used for interpretation. The case where "23:58" gets assigned to the next day when processing happens after midnight is an inherent limitation of time-only logs, but it's better than the current behavior which produces non-monotonic timestamps.

Actually, wait. Let me think about this differently. The PR says the expected behavior is that all entries should be assigned to March 30 (the correct date). The current behavior gives:
- 23:58 → March 30 ✓
- 00:00 → March 30 (local), but March 29 (UTC) — PR says this is "March 29"

The PR author seems to care about the UTC date being March 29 for the 00:00 entry. They want it to be March 30.

But March 30, 00:00 CEST is ALWAYS March 29, 22:00 UTC. You can't change that without changing the timezone offset.

UNLESS... the issue is different. Let me re-read the PR one more time:

"Times just after midnight (00:00–02:00) are assigned to the previous day instead of the current one."

Maybe "assigned to the previous day" means the local date is wrong? Let me check the local dates in the current output:
- 23:58 → March 30 local ✓
- 00:00 → March 30 local ✓
- 02:00 → March 30 local ✓

All local dates are March 30! So the local dates are correct. The UTC dates differ. But the PR says "assigned to the previous day" — maybe they're looking at the UTC date?

Or maybe the issue is specifically about how the date is displayed/reported in their downstream system (OpenSearch), which might use UTC.

Let me check if there's something else going on. Let me look at the actual flb_parser_time_lookup function more carefully:

```c
if (parser->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
    ...
    gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
    
    /* Make the timestamp default to today */
    tm->tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
    tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
    
    uint64_t t = tmy.tm_year + 1900;
    
    fmt = tmp;
    u64_to_str(t, fmt);
    fmt += 4;
    *fmt++ = ' ';
    
    memcpy(fmt, time_ptr, time_len);
    fmt += time_len;
    *fmt++ = '\0';
    
    time_ptr = tmp;
    time_len = strlen(tmp);
    p = flb_strptime(time_ptr, parser->time_fmt_year, tm);
}
```

Wait, it only sets `tm_mon` and `tm_mday`. What about `tm_year`? It prepends the year to the time string and parses with `time_fmt_year` which is `%Y %H:%M:%S`. The year comes from the string prepending, not from `tm->tm.tm_year`.

But `tm->tm.tm_year` is NOT set from `tmy.tm_year` before parsing! Let me check... 

After `flb_strptime` parses `"2026 00:00:00"` with format `"%Y %H:%M:%S"`, it will set `tm->tm.tm_year`, `tm->tm.tm_hour`, `tm->tm.tm_min`, `tm->tm.tm_sec`. But `tm->tm.tm_mon` and `tm->tm.tm_mday` are set BEFORE parsing (lines 1205-1206). So the year comes from the string, and month/day come from `gmtime_r`.

OK so the logic is:
1. Get current UTC date (year, month, day) from `gmtime_r`
2. Set month and day from UTC date
3. Prepend year to time string and parse
4. The parsed result has: year from string (= UTC year), month from UTC date, day from UTC date, hour/min/sec from the log

Then `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` calls `mktime`, which interprets this as local time.

So the inconsistency is: year, month, day are from UTC, but `mktime` interprets as local. 

The fix: when `time_system_timezone` is true, use `localtime_r` to get year, month, day. This ensures consistency.

Let me now implement the fix

{
    int ret;
    time_t time_now;
    char *p = NULL;
    char *fmt;
    int time_len = tsize;
    const char *time_ptr = time_str;
    char tmp[64];
    struct tm tmy;

    *ns = 0;

    if (tsize > sizeof(tmp) - 1) {
        flb_error("[parser] time string length is too long");
        return -1;
    }

    /*
     * Some records coming from old Syslog messages do not contain the
     * year, so it'"'"'s required to ingest this information in the value
     * to be parsed.
     */
    if (parser->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
        /* Given time string is too long */
        if (time_len + 6 >= sizeof(tmp)) {
            return -1;
        }

        }

            time_now = now;
        }

                           time_t now,
                           struct flb_parser *parser,
                           struct flb_tm *tm, double *ns)
{
    int ret;
    time_t time_now;
    char *p = NULL;
    char *fmt;
    int time_len = tsize;
    const char *time_ptr = time_str;
    char tmp[64];
    struct tm tmy;

    *ns = 0;

    if (tsize > sizeof(tmp) - 1) {
        flb_error("[parser] time string length is too long");
        return -1;
    }

    /*
     * Some records coming from old Syslog messages do not contain the
     * year, so it'"'"'s required to ingest this information in the value
     * to be parsed.
     */
    if (parser->time_with_year == FLB_FALSE) {
        /* Given time string is too long */
        if (time_len + 6 >= sizeof(tmp)) {
            return -1;
        }

        /*
         * This is not the most elegant way but for now it let
         * get the work done.
         */
        if (now <= 0) {
            time_now = time(NULL);
        }
        else {
            time_now = now;
        }

        /*
         * If the system timezone fallback is enabled, use localtime_r
         * to determine the current date so that it matches the timezone
         * that will be used by mktime(3) in flb_parser_tm2time.
         * Otherwise, use gmtime_r for UTC-based date assignment.
         */
        if (parser->time_system_timezone) {
            localtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
        }
        else {
            gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
        }

        /* Make the timestamp default to today */
        tm->tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
        tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;

        uint64_t t = tmy.tm_year + 1900;

        fmt = tmp;
        u64_to_str(t, fmt);
        fmt += 4;
        *fmt++ = '"'"' '"'"';

        memcpy(fmt, time_ptr, time_len);
        fmt += time_len;
        *fmt++ = '"'"'\0'"'"';

        time_ptr = tmp;
        time_len = strlen(tmp);
        p = flb_strptime(time_ptr, parser->time_fmt_year, tm);
    }'

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_fix.c << 'EOF'
#include <stdio.h>
#include <time.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

/* Minimal reproduction using the actual fix logic */

/* Copy the flb_tm structure */
struct flb_tm {
    struct tm tm;
    long int tm_gmtoff;
};
#define flb_tm_gmtoff(x) (x)->tm_gmtoff

static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
                                        int use_system_timezone)
{
    struct tm tmp;
    time_t res;

    tmp = src->tm;
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
        res = mktime(&tmp);
    } else {
        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    }
    return res;
}

void simulate_parse(const char *time_str, time_t now, int use_system_timezone) {
    struct flb_tm tm;
    struct tm tmy;
    time_t result;
    
    memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
    
    /* Simulate the fixed flb_parser_time_lookup */
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        localtime_r(&now, &tmy);
    } else {
        gmtime_r(&now, &tmy);
    }
    
    tm.tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
    tm.tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
    
    int hour, min, sec;
    sscanf(time_str, "%d:%d:%d", &hour, &min, &sec);
    tm.tm.tm_hour = hour;
    tm.tm.tm_min = min;
    tm.tm.tm_sec = sec;
    
    /* The year would be prepended by the actual code, but we set it manually */
    tm.tm.tm_year = tmy.tm_year;
    
    result = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, use_system_timezone);
    
    char utc_buf[64], local_buf[64];
    time_t tmp_time = result;
    strftime(utc_buf, sizeof(utc_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S UTC", gmtime(&tmp_time));
    tmp_time = result;
    strftime(local_buf, sizeof(local_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S %Z", localtime(&tmp_time));
    
    printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld\n    UTC:   %s\n    local: %s\n",
           time_str, result, utc_buf, local_buf);
}

int main() {
    time_t now;
    
    /* Set timezone to Europe/Stockholm */
    setenv("TZ", "Europe/Stockholm", 1);
    tzset();
    
    printf("Timezone: %s\n\n", getenv("TZ"));
    
    /* Test 1: Processing happens at March 30, 22:00 UTC = March 31, 00:00 local */
    struct tm base = {0};
    base.tm_year = 2026 - 1900;
    base.tm_mon = 2;
    base.tm_mday = 30;
    base.tm_hour = 22;
    base.tm_min = 0;
    base.tm_sec = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("=== Test 1: Processing at midnight (March 31, 00:00 local) ===\n");
    printf("Now: %s", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    printf("\nWith time_system_timezone=OFF (gmtime_r):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 0);
    
    printf("\nWith time_system_timezone=ON (localtime_r - FIXED):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1);
    
    /* Test 2: Processing happens at March 30, 21:00 UTC = March 30, 23:00 local */
    base.tm_hour = 21;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("\n=== Test 2: Processing before midnight (March 30, 23:00 local) ===\n");
    printf("Now: %s", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    printf("\nWith time_system_timezone=OFF (gmtime_r):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 0);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 0);
    
    printf("\nWith time_system_timezone=ON (localtime_r - FIXED):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1);
    
    /* Test 3: Edge case - UTC- timezone (e.g., America/New_York) */
    setenv("TZ", "America/New_York", 1);
    tzset();
    
    printf("\n=== Test 3: America/New_York (UTC-5) ===\n");
    /* Processing at April 1, 2026 04:00 UTC = March 31, 23:00 local (EST) */
    base.tm_mon = 3; /* April */
    base.tm_mday = 1;
    base.tm_hour = 4;
    base.tm_min = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("Now: %s", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    printf("Now (UTC): %s", asctime(gmtime(&now)));
    
    printf("With time_system_timezone=ON (localtime_r - FIXED):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1);
    
    return 0;
}

Hmm, there are issues with both approaches. Let me analyze:

**Test 2 (before midnight, March 30, 23:00 local):**

With the fix (time_system_timezone=ON, localtime_r):
- 23:58 → March 30, 23:58 CEST ✓ (epoch=1774907880, local: March 30 23:58)
- 23:59 → March 30, 23:59 CEST ✓
- 00:00 → March 30, 00:00 CEST ✓ (epoch=1774821600, local: March 30 00:00)
- 00:01 → March 30, 00:01 CEST ✓
- 02:00 → March 30, 02:00 CEST ✓

All on March 30 local time! The epochs are monotonic:
- 00:00 (1774821600) < 00:01 (1774821660) < 02:00 (1774828800) < 23:58 (1774907880) < 23:59 (1774907940)

This is CORRECT! The fix works for Test 2.

But wait, let me check the OLD code (time_system_timezone=OFF) for Test 2:
- 23:58 → epoch=1774915080, local: March 31, 01:58 CEST ← WRONG! Should be March 30, 23:58

That's because `gmtime_r` gives March 30, but `timegm` interprets as UTC. Actually wait, `time_system_timezone=OFF` uses `timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src)`. Since `gmtoff` is 0 (no timezone in format and time_offset=0), it just uses `timegm`. So March 30, 23:58 interpreted as UTC = March 30, 23:58 UTC = March 31, 01:58 CEST. That's wrong for local time interpretation.

But the PR is about `time_system_timezone=ON`, so the OFF case is not relevant here.

**Test 1 (after midnight, March 31, 00:00 local):**

With the fix (time_system_timezone=ON, localtime_r):
- 23:58 → March 31, 23:58 CEST (epoch=1774994280)
- 00:00 → March 31, 00:00 CEST (epoch=1774908000)

The epochs: 00:00 (1774908000) < 02:00 (1774915200) < 23:58 (1774994280). Monotonic! ✓

But the date for 23:58 is March 31, which is "tomorrow" relative to the expected March 30. However, this is because processing happens after midnight — the code assumes today is March 31, so 23:58 must be March 31.

Now compare with the OLD code (gmtime_r):
- 23:58 → epoch=1774915080, local: March 31, 01:58 CEST
- 00:00 → epoch=1774828800, local: March 30, 02:00 CEST

The epochs: 00:00 (1774828800) < 23:58 (1774915080). Also monotonic! But the local times are wrong: 23:58 becomes 01:58, and 00:00 becomes 02:00.

Wait, the old code with `time_system_timezone=OFF` is clearly wrong for both cases. Let me check the OLD code with `time_system_timezone=ON` (which is the actual bug scenario):

Actually, my test above for "time_system_timezone=OFF" uses `use_system_timezone=0` in `flb_parser_tm2time`, which is `timegm`. But the PR scenario uses `time_system_timezone=ON`, which corresponds to `use_system_timezone=1` (mktime).

Let me re-run with the correct combination: OLD code = gmtime_r + mktime, NEW code = localtime_r + mktime.

cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_fix2.c << 'EOF'
#include <stdio.h>
#include <time.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>

struct flb_tm {
    struct tm tm;
    long int tm_gmtoff;
};
#define flb_tm_gmtoff(x) (x)->tm_gmtoff

static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
                                        int use_system_timezone)
{
    struct tm tmp;
    time_t res;
    tmp = src->tm;
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
        res = mktime(&tmp);
    } else {
        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    }
    return res;
}

void simulate_parse(const char *time_str, time_t now, int use_system_timezone, int use_localtime_for_date) {
    struct flb_tm tm;
    struct tm tmy;
    time_t result;
    
    memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
    
    if (use_localtime_for_date) {
        localtime_r(&now, &tmy);
    } else {
        gmtime_r(&now, &tmy);
    }
    
    tm.tm.tm_mon = tmy.tm_mon;
    tm.tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
    tm.tm.tm_year = tmy.tm_year;
    
    int hour, min, sec;
    sscanf(time_str, "%d:%d:%d", &hour, &min, &sec);
    tm.tm.tm_hour = hour;
    tm.tm.tm_min = min;
    tm.tm.tm_sec = sec;
    
    result = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, use_system_timezone);
    
    char local_buf[64];
    time_t tmp_time = result;
    strftime(local_buf, sizeof(local_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S %Z", localtime(&tmp_time));
    
    printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (%s)\n", time_str, result, local_buf);
}

int main() {
    time_t now;
    
    setenv("TZ", "Europe/Stockholm", 1);
    tzset();
    printf("Timezone: %s\n\n", getenv("TZ"));
    
    /* Test 1: Processing at March 30, 22:00 UTC = March 31, 00:00 local */
    struct tm base = {0};
    base.tm_year = 2026 - 1900;
    base.tm_mon = 2;
    base.tm_mday = 30;
    base.tm_hour = 22;
    base.tm_min = 0;
    base.tm_sec = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("=== Test 1: Processing at midnight (March 31, 00:00 local) ===\n");
    printf("Now local: %s\n", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    printf("\nOLD code (gmtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    
    printf("\nNEW code (localtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    
    /* Test 2: Processing before midnight */
    base.tm_hour = 21;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("\n=== Test 2: Processing before midnight (March 30, 23:00 local) ===\n");
    printf("Now local: %s\n", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    printf("\nOLD code (gmtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    
    printf("\nNEW code (localtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    
    /* Test 3: Processing at March 30, 20:00 UTC = March 30, 22:00 local */
    base.tm_hour = 20;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("\n=== Test 3: Processing at March 30, 22:00 local ===\n");
    printf("Now local: %s\n", asctime(localtime(&now)));
    
    printf("\nOLD code (gmtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 0);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 0);
    
    printf("\nNEW code (localtime_r + mktime):\n");
    simulate_parse("23:58:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("23:59:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("00:01:00", now, 1, 1);
    simulate_parse("02:00:00", now, 1, 1);
    
    return 0;
}

So the fundamental issue is: you can't have March 30, 23:58 and March 30, 00:00 on the same day and expect the epochs to be monotonic with the chronological order. 00:00 will always be before 23:58 on the same day.

The only way to make epochs monotonic with chronological order is:
- 23:58 on March 30
- 00:00 on March 31 (next day, since it's after midnight)

But that means 00:00 is assigned to the next day. The PR author says they want all entries on March 30. But that's impossible if you also want monotonic epochs in chronological order.

Let me look at the actual problem from the code perspective:

The issue is that `gmtime_r` returns UTC date, but `mktime` interprets as local time. This mismatch causes problems when UTC and local dates differ.

My fix (using `localtime_r` when `time_system_timezone` is on) addresses this mismatch. Let me verify that the fix is correct by running the actual test suite again and also checking if there are any other places that need changes.

But first, let me think about edge cases:

1. **Negative UTC offsets** (e.g., America/New_York, UTC-5): When local time is 23:00 on day D, UTC is 04:00 on day D+1. With `gmtime_r`, the date would be D+1 (UTC), but `mktime` interprets as local (day D). This would cause the opposite problem: times get assigned to the NEXT day instead of the current day. My fix should handle this correctly by using `localtime_r`.

2. **DST transitions**: When DST changes, the local time jumps forward or backward. `mktime` handles this with `tm_isdst = -1`. Using `localtime_r` should give the correct local date.

3. **Timezones with no DST** (e.g., UTC): When timezone is UTC, `gmtime_r` and `localtime_r` return the same thing, so the fix has no effect.

4. **`time_system_timezone` OFF**: The old behavior is preserved (using `gmtime_r`).

Let me also check if there's another issue: the `flb_parser_tm2time` function's non-system-timezone path might also have issues. When `use_system_timezone` is false:

```c
res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
```

This converts to UTC using `timegm` and then subtracts the gmtoff. But if the time was parsed with a timezone in the string (like `%z`), `gmtoff` is set correctly. If not, `gmtoff` is set to `parser->time_offset` (which defaults to 0). This path doesn't seem affected by our change.
