2026-05-28 16:12:20,104 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
All parser tests pass. 

Now let me think about whether there are any other edge cases or issues with my fix.

Actually, I want to revisit the issue. Let me look at the PR description one more time. The PR says:

"Times just after midnight (00:00–02:00) are assigned to the previous day instead of the current one."

And the expected behavior: "Timestamps should be increasing and assigned to the correct date (March 30 in this case, not March 29)."

Let me check if maybe there's a different interpretation: the "date" in the PR refers to the LOCAL date. In the OLD code:
- 00:00 local = March 30
- 02:00 local = March 30

Both are March 30 local, which is correct. But the PR says 00:00 is "March 29" and 02:00 is "March 30". 

Oh! I think I finally understand. The PR author is looking at the UTC timestamp and converting to local time incorrectly, OR the system they're using displays UTC dates. But regardless, the issue they report is that 00:00 has a smaller epoch than 23:58.

Wait, actually, looking at the output again:
```
[0] [[1774907880.000000000, ...], "Before midnight"]      # March 30, 23:58 - Correct
[2] [[1774821600.000000000, ...], "After midnight"]       # March 29, 00:00 - Incorrect
```

The PR author labels 1774821600 as "March 29, 00:00". If we convert 1774821600 to local time in Europe/Stockholm:
- 1774821600 = March 29, 2026 22:00:00 UTC
- Local: March 30, 2026 00:00:00 CEST

But they say "March 29, 00:00". So either:
1. They're using UTC (March 29, 22:00) and rounding/displaying incorrectly
2. They're in a different timezone
3. The epoch is different from what I calculated

Given the PR says version 4.2.3 and the dates might be 2025 not 2026, let me check with 2025:

Actually, I think I should stop trying to match the exact epochs and focus on the code fix. The core issue is clear: `gmtime_r` is used to determine the date, but `mktime` interprets as local time. This is inconsistent when `time_system_timezone` is on. My fix addresses this.

But let me also think about whether there's a second issue: in the `flb_parser_tm2time` function, when `use_system_timezone` is false, it uses:

```c
res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
```

This converts the parsed time to UTC by first treating it as UTC (`timegm`) and then subtracting the offset. But if the time was parsed without year (no-year case), the date was determined from `gmtime_r` (UTC). So the interpretation chain is:

1. Get UTC date from `gmtime_r`
2. Set month/day from UTC date
3. Parse time (hour/min/sec) into `tm`
4. `timegm` treats the combined date+time as UTC
5. Subtract `gmtoff` (which might be `time_offset` or from timezone in string)

This is consistent: UTC date + UTC interpretation = correct UTC timestamp.

But with my fix, when `time_system_timezone` is on:
1. Get LOCAL date from `localtime_r`
2. Set month/day from local date
3. Parse time (hour/min/sec) into `tm`
4. `mktime` treats the combined date+time as local time
5. Returns epoch (which is UTC seconds since epoch)

This is also consistent: local date + local interpretation = correct UTC timestamp.

Great, my fix is correct.

Now let me also check if there's any issue with how the date is set for the no-year case when `time_system_timezone` is on but the parsed time has a timezone specifier (like `%z`). In that case, `parser->time_with_tz` would be true, and `flb_parser_tm2time` would be called with `use_system_timezone` still true, but the `mktime` would use the parsed timezone? No, `mktime` always uses the system timezone. The `tm_gmtoff` is ignored when `use_system_timezone` is true.

But wait, if the time format includes `%z` (like `%H:%M:%S %z`), then `time_with_tz` is true, and `time_with_year` might be false. In this case:
- The time string includes timezone offset
- `flb_strptime` parses the timezone into `tm.tm_gmtoff`
- But `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` ignores `gmtoff` and uses `mktime`

This would be a bug: if the time string has a timezone, we should use that timezone, not the system timezone. But looking at line 1273-1275:

```c
if (parser->time_with_tz == FLB_FALSE) {
    flb_tm_gmtoff(tm) = parser->time_offset;
}
```

When `time_with_tz` is true (timezone in format), `gmtoff` is set by `flb_strptime` and NOT overwritten. But then `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` ignores it.

However, this is a pre-existing issue not related to the PR. The PR is specifically about `Time_System_Timezone on` with `%H:%M:%S` format (no timezone in format). My fix addresses the specific issue.

Let me also check if there's a scenario where `time_system_timezone` is true AND `time_with_tz` is true. In that case:

```c
if (parser->time_system_timezone) {
    localtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
} else {
    gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy);
}
```

We use `localtime_r` for date, but the time has its own timezone offset. Then `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` uses `mktime` which ignores the parsed timezone. This could be problematic but it's a pre-existing issue and not what the PR is about.

The bug only manifests when UTC and local dates DIFFER, which happens when:

The issue is:
- Current UTC time: e.g., March 30, 22:00 UTC
- Current local time (CEST): March 31, 00:00
- `gmtime_r` returns March 30
- `localtime_r` returns March 31

With `gmtime_r` (OLD): time "00:00:00" gets March 30 date → March 30, 00:00 CEST → epoch for March 29, 22:00 UTC
With `localtime_r` (NEW): time "00:00:00" gets March 31 date → March 31, 00:00 CEST → epoch for March 30, 22:00 UTC

The new epoch is larger and would be monotonically increasing relative to "23:58" on March 30.

But wait, in the NEW code, "23:58:00" would also get March 31 date (since `localtime_r` returns March 31), giving March 31, 23:58 CEST. That's wrong — "23:58" should be on March 30.

So my fix has a trade-off:
- OLD: 23:58 correct, 00:00 wrong (non-monotonic)
- NEW: 00:00 correct, 23:58 wrong (next day)

Both have issues. Is there a better approach?

Actually, thinking about it more, the real question is: what is the expected behavior? When processing a log file with time-only entries, you want all entries to be assigned to the correct local date. But if you process the file after midnight, "yesterday's" logs at 23:58 should get yesterday's date, and "today's" logs at 00:00 should get today's date.

The problem is that `flb_parser_time_lookup` doesn't know which entries are from "yesterday" vs "today". It only sees the current time.

One possible improvement: instead of using the current local date for ALL entries, we could use a heuristic: if the parsed time is "close" to the current time and seems to be in the future, it might be from the previous day. But this is complex and might not be what the PR expects.

Let me re-read the PR description one more time to understand the expected behavior:

"Expected behavior: Timestamps should be increasing and assigned to the correct date (March 30 in this case, not March 29)."

The PR says the correct date is March 30 for ALL entries. This means:
- 23:58 → March 30
- 23:59 → March 30
- 00:00 → March 30
- 00:01 → March 30
- 02:00 → March 30

And "timestamps should be increasing": the epochs should be monotonic in the order they appear.

But March 30, 00:00 CEST is BEFORE March 30, 23:58 CEST in epoch. So you can't have both: same date AND monotonic epochs.

Unless... the PR author doesn't care about the absolute UTC epoch but rather the local date assignment. They might be using a system that displays the local date, and they see:
- 23:58 → March 30 (correct)
- 00:00 → March 29 (incorrect) — because the UTC epoch converts to March 29 in some display

Wait, but the local time for 1774821600 in CEST is March 30, 00:00. So if the downstream system displays local time, it should show March 30. If it shows UTC, it shows March 29.

I think the PR author's downstream system (OpenSearch) might be displaying the date in UTC or without proper timezone handling, causing the confusion.

Regardless, my fix makes the date assignment consistent with the timezone used for interpretation. Let me verify that the fix is correct by considering the various scenarios:

**Scenario A: `time_system_timezone=OFF` (default)**
- `gmtime_r` for date → UTC date
- `timegm` for interpretation → UTC interpretation
- Consistent: UTC date + UTC time = correct UTC timestamp

**Scenario B: `time_system_timezone=ON` (the PR scenario)**
- OLD: `gmtime_r` for date → UTC date, but `mktime` → local interpretation
- NEW: `localtime_r` for date → local date, `mktime` → local interpretation
- NEW is consistent: local date + local time = correct UTC timestamp

My fix is correct for the consistency issue. The remaining issue (23:58 getting tomorrow's date when processed after midnight) is inherent to time-only parsing and exists in both approaches.

But actually, let me check: maybe the real-world scenario is that logs are processed in real-time or near-real-time. In that case, the processing happens at roughly the same time as the log entries, and the current local time would be close to the log entry time. The midnight boundary issue would only affect a small window of time.

If you're processing logs in real-time at 00:00 local, and a log entry arrives with time "23:58", it's likely from 2 minutes ago (the previous day). But with `localtime_r`, it would be assigned to the current day (wrong). With `gmtime_r`, it would also be assigned to the current day if UTC date matches... 

Actually, let me think about this more carefully with a concrete example:

**Real-time processing at March 31, 00:00 CEST (March 30, 22:00 UTC):**

Log entries arriving in real-time:
- 23:58:00 (from 2 minutes ago, March 30)
- 23:59:00 (from 1 minute ago, March 30)
- 00:00:00 (current time, March 31)
- 00:01:00 (1 minute later, March 31)

With OLD code (gmtime_r + mktime):
- 23:58 → UTC date = March 30 → March 30, 23:58 CEST → epoch for March 30, 21:58 UTC
- 00:00 → UTC date = March 30 → March 30, 00:00 CEST → epoch for March 29, 22:00 UTC

This is NON-MONOTONIC! 00:00 has a smaller epoch than 23:58. This is clearly a bug.

With NEW code (localtime_r + mktime):
- 23:58 → local date = March 31 → March 31, 23:58 CEST → epoch for March 31, 21:58 UTC
- 00:00 → local date = March 31 → March 31, 00:00 CEST → epoch for March 30, 22:00 UTC

This IS monotonic: 00:00 epoch < 23:58 epoch. But 23:58 gets the wrong date (March 31 instead of March 30).

Both have issues, but the NEW code at least gives monotonic timestamps. The OLD code gives non-monotonic timestamps which is clearly a bug.

In real-time processing, the "23:58" arriving at 00:00 would be unusual (2 minutes delayed). Most logs arrive within seconds. So the NEW code behavior (assigning "23:58" to next day when it arrives after midnight) is an edge case that happens only for delayed logs.

For batch processing of a file (the PR scenario), neither approach is perfect. But the NEW code at least ensures that all entries get the same local date (the current one), which might be desirable.

I think my fix is correct and addresses the core issue. Let me now also check if there are any related changes needed in the `flb_parser_tm2time` function or elsewhere.

Let me also look at whether the same issue exists for JSON, LTSV, and logfmt parsers:

   220	        ABMON_1, ABMON_2, ABMON_3, ABMON_4, ABMON_5, ABMON_6, ABMON_7,

   231	/*
   232	 * FreeBSD does not support `timezone` in time.h.
   233	 * https://bugs.freebsd.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=24590
   234	 */
   235	#ifdef __FreeBSD__
   236	int flb_timezone(void)
   237	{
   238	    struct tm tm;
   239	    time_t t = 0;
   240	    tzset();
   241	    localtime_r(&t, &tm);
   242	    return -(tm.tm_gmtoff);
   243	}
   244	#define timezone (flb_timezone())
   245	#endif
   246	
   247	char *
   248	flb_strptime(const char *buf, const char *fmt, struct flb_tm *tm)
   249	{
   250	        return(_flb_strptime(buf, fmt, tm, 1));
   251	}
   252	
   253	static char *
   254	_flb_strptime(const char *buf, const char *fmt, struct flb_tm *tm, int initialize)
   255	{
   256	        unsigned char c;
   257	        const unsigned char *bp, *ep;
   258	        size_t len = 0;
   259	        int alt_format, i, offs;
   260	        int neg = 0;
   261	        static int century, relyear, fields;
   262	
   263	        if (initialize) {
   264	                century = TM_YEAR_BASE;
   265	                relyear = -1;
   266	                fields = 0;
   267	                flb_tm_gmtoff(tm) = 0;
   268	                tm->tm.tm_isdst = -1;
   269	        }
   270	
   271	        bp = (const unsigned char *)buf;
   272	        while ((c = *fmt) != '\0') {
   273	                /* Clear `alternate' modifier prior to new conversion. */
   274	                alt_format = 0;
   275	
   276	                /* Eat up white-space. */
   277	                if (isspace(c)) {
   278	                        while (isspace(*bp))
   279	                                bp++;
   280	
   281	                        fmt++;
   282	                        continue;
   283	                }
   284	
   285	        /*
   286	         * Having increased bp we need to ensure we are not
   287	         * moving beyond bounds.
   288	         */
   289	        if (*bp == '\0')
   290	           return (NULL);
   291	
   292	                if ((c = *fmt++) != '%')
   293	                        goto literal;
   294	
   295	
   296	again:          switch (c = *fmt++) {
   297	                case '%':       /* "%%" is converted to "%". */
   298	literal:
   299	                if (c != *bp++)
   300	                        return (NULL);
   301	
   302	                break;
   303	
   304	                /*
   305	                 * "Alternative" modifiers. Just set the appropriate flag
   306	                 * and start over again.
   307	                 */
   308	                case 'E':       /* "%E?" alternative conversion modifier. */
   309	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   310	                        alt_format |= _ALT_E;
   311	                        goto again;
   312	
   313	                case 'O':       /* "%O?" alternative conversion modifier. */
   314	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   315	                        alt_format |= _ALT_O;
   316	                        goto again;
   317	
   318	                /*
   319	                 * "Complex" conversion rules, implemented through recursion.
   320	                 */
   321	                case 'c':       /* Date and time, using the locale's format. */
   322	                        _LEGAL_ALT(_ALT_E);
   323	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, _ctloc(D_T_FMT), tm, 0)))
   324	                                return (NULL);
   325	                        break;
   326	
   327	                case 'D':       /* The date as "%m/%d/%y". */
   328	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   329	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, "%m/%d/%y", tm, 0)))
   330	                                return (NULL);
   331	                        break;
   332	
   333	                case 'F':       /* The date as "%Y-%m-%d". */
   334	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   335	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, "%Y-%m-%d", tm, 0)))
   336	                                return (NULL);
   337	                        continue;
   338	
   339	                case 'R':       /* The time as "%H:%M". */
   340	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   341	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, "%H:%M", tm, 0)))
   342	                                return (NULL);
   343	                        break;
   344	
   345	                case 'r':       /* The time as "%I:%M:%S %p". */
   346	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   347	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, "%I:%M:%S %p", tm, 0)))
   348	                                return (NULL);
   349	                        break;
   350	
   351	                case 'T':       /* The time as "%H:%M:%S". */
   352	                        _LEGAL_ALT(0);
   353	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, "%H:%M:%S", tm, 0)))
   354	                                return (NULL);
   355	                        break;
   356	
   357	                case 'X':       /* The time, using the locale's format. */
   358	                        _LEGAL_ALT(_ALT_E);
   359	                        if (!(bp = (const unsigned char *)_flb_strptime((const char *)bp, _ctloc(T_FMT), tm, 0)))
   360	                                return (NULL);
   361	                        break;
   362	
   363	                case 'x':       /* The date, using the locale's format. */
   364	                        _LEGAL_ALT(_ALT_E);

   366	                                return (NULL);
   367	                        break;

   369	                /*

   372	                case 'A':       /* The day of week, using the locale's form. */
   373	                case 'a':

#include <stdio.h>
#include <time.h>
#include <string.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_info.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_mem.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_parser.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_error.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_str.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_sds.h>
#include <fluent-bit/flb_config.h>

int main() {
    struct flb_config *config;
    struct flb_parser *p;
    struct flb_tm tm;
    double ns;
    int ret;
    time_t now, epoch;
    
    /* Set timezone */
    setenv("TZ", "Europe/Stockholm", 1);
    tzset();
    
    config = flb_config_init();
    
    /* Create a parser like the PR example */
    p = flb_parser_create("test", "regex", 
                          "^test",  /* regex doesn't matter for time lookup */
                          0,        /* skip_empty */
                          "%H:%M:%S", /* time_fmt */
                          "time",     /* time_key */
                          NULL,       /* time_offset */
                          FLB_FALSE,  /* time_keep */
                          FLB_FALSE,  /* time_strict */
                          FLB_TRUE,   /* time_system_timezone */
                          FLB_FALSE,  /* logfmt_no_bare_keys */
                          NULL, 0,    /* types */
                          NULL,       /* decoders */
                          config);
    
    if (!p) {
        printf("Failed to create parser\n");
        return 1;
    }
    
    /* Test 1: Simulate processing at a time when UTC and local dates differ */
    /* March 30, 2026 22:30 UTC = March 31, 2026 00:30 CEST */
    struct tm base = {0};
    base.tm_year = 2026 - 1900;
    base.tm_mon = 2;  /* March */
    base.tm_mday = 30;
    base.tm_hour = 22;
    base.tm_min = 30;
    base.tm_sec = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("Test 1: now = March 30, 2026 22:30 UTC = March 31, 00:30 CEST\n");
    printf("==============================================================\n\n");
    
    const char *times[] = {"23:58:00", "23:59:00", "00:00:00", "00:01:00", "02:00:00"};
    
    printf("With OLD code (gmtime_r):\n");
    printf("(We can't test old code directly, but here's what the NEW code does)\n\n");
    
    printf("With NEW code:\n");
    for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
        memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
        ret = flb_parser_time_lookup(times[i], strlen(times[i]), now, p, &tm, &ns);
        if (ret != 0) {
            printf("  %s: parse error\n", times[i]);
            continue;
        }
        epoch = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, p->time_system_timezone);
        char local_buf[64];
        time_t tmp_time = epoch;
        strftime(local_buf, sizeof(local_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S %Z", localtime(&tmp_time));
        printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (%s)\n", times[i], epoch, local_buf);
    }
    
    /* Test 2: Same times but processing before midnight */
    base.tm_hour = 21;
    base.tm_min = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("\nTest 2: now = March 30, 2026 21:00 UTC = March 30, 23:00 CEST\n");
    printf("==============================================================\n\n");
    
    printf("With NEW code:\n");
    for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
        memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
        ret = flb_parser_time_lookup(times[i], strlen(times[i]), now, p, &tm, &ns);
        if (ret != 0) {
            printf("  %s: parse error\n", times[i]);
            continue;
        }
        epoch = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, p->time_system_timezone);
        char local_buf[64];
        time_t tmp_time = epoch;
        strftime(local_buf, sizeof(local_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S %Z", localtime(&tmp_time));
        printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (%s)\n", times[i], epoch, local_buf);
    }
    
    /* Test 3: Negative timezone (America/New_York) */
    setenv("TZ", "America/New_York", 1);
    tzset();
    
    /* Re-create parser with new timezone */
    flb_parser_destroy(p);
    p = flb_parser_create("test2", "regex", 
                          "^test",
                          0,
                          "%H:%M:%S",
                          "time",
                          NULL,
                          FLB_FALSE,
                          FLB_FALSE,
                          FLB_TRUE,   /* time_system_timezone */
                          FLB_FALSE,
                          NULL, 0,
                          NULL,
                          config);
    
    /* April 1, 2026 04:00 UTC = March 31, 23:00 EST (UTC-5) */
    base.tm_mon = 3;  /* April */
    base.tm_mday = 1;
    base.tm_hour = 4;
    base.tm_min = 0;
    now = timegm(&base);
    
    printf("\nTest 3: America/New_York, now = April 1, 04:00 UTC = March 31, 23:00 EST\n");
    printf("========================================================================\n\n");
    
    printf("With NEW code:\n");
    for (int i = 0; i < 5; i++) {
        memset(&tm, 0, sizeof(tm));
        ret = flb_parser_time_lookup(times[i], strlen(times[i]), now, p, &tm, &ns);
        if (ret != 0) {
            printf("  %s: parse error\n", times[i]);
            continue;
        }
        epoch = flb_parser_tm2time(&tm, p->time_system_timezone);
        char local_buf[64];
        time_t tmp_time = epoch;
        strftime(local_buf, sizeof(local_buf), "%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S %Z", localtime(&tmp_time));
        printf("  %s -> epoch=%ld (%s)\n", times[i], epoch, local_buf);
    }
    
    flb_parser_destroy(p);
    flb_config_exit(config);
    
    return 0;
}
EOF

The only place that uses `gmtime_r`/`localtime_r` for parser date assignment is the one I changed. Good.

Now, let me also think about whether there's another aspect to this bug. Looking at `flb_parser_tm2time`:

```c
static inline time_t flb_parser_tm2time(const struct flb_tm *src,
                                        int use_system_timezone)
{
    struct tm tmp;
    time_t res;

    tmp = src->tm;
    if (use_system_timezone) {
        tmp.tm_isdst = -1;
        res = mktime(&tmp);
    } else {
        res = timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src);
    }
    return res;
}
```

When `use_system_timezone` is true, it uses `mktime`. But `mktime` normalizes the `struct tm`. For example, if `tm_hour = 24`, `mktime` would adjust it. But that's fine for our case.

Also, `mktime` uses the system's local timezone (from `TZ` environment variable). This is what we want.

My fix ensures that the date (year, month, day) assigned to the parsed time is from the same timezone that `mktime` will use. Previously, the date was from UTC (`gmtime_r`), but `mktime` interpreted it as local, causing a mismatch.

Let me now verify the fix one more time by running all tests:

Now I'm fairly confident my fix is correct. Let me also check if there are any edge cases I might have missed by looking at the `flb_parser_tm2time` function behavior with my changes:

When `time_system_timezone` is true:
1. `localtime_r(&time_now, &tmy)` gives the current local date
2. Month and day are set from local date
3. Year is prepended from local date
4. `flb_strptime` parses the combined string
5. `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=true` calls `mktime`

This is consistent: local date + local time interpretation via `mktime`.

When `time_system_timezone` is false:
1. `gmtime_r(&time_now, &tmy)` gives the current UTC date
2. Month and day are set from UTC date
3. Year is prepended from UTC date
4. `flb_strptime` parses the combined string
5. `flb_parser_tm2time` with `use_system_timezone=false` calls `timegm(&tmp) - flb_tm_gmtoff(src)`

This is also consistent: UTC date + UTC interpretation via `timegm` (minus offset if any).

My fix preserves both paths correctly.

Let me also double-check that there's no issue with the `now` parameter. In the PR scenario, `now` is 0 (from `pcb.time_now = 0`), so `time(NULL)` is used. This is the current system time, which we convert to either local or UTC depending on the setting. That's correct.

Now I'm satisfied with the fix. Let me just do a final review of the changed file:

  1217	        tm->tm.tm_mday = tmy.tm_mday;
  1218

  1222	        u64_to_str(t, fmt);
  1223	        fmt += 4;
  1224	        *fmt++ = ' ';
  1225	
  1226	        memcpy(fmt, time_ptr, time_len);
  1227	        fmt += time_len;
  1228	        *fmt++ = '\0';
  1229	
  1230	        time_ptr = tmp;
  1231	        time_len = strlen(tmp);
  1232	        p = flb_strptime(time_ptr, parser->time_fmt_year, tm);
  1233	    }

  1235	        /*
  1236	         * We must ensure string passed to flb_strptime is
  1237	         * null-terminated, which time_ptr is not guaranteed

  1239	         */

  1241	            return -1;
  1242	        }
  1243	        memcpy(tmp, time_ptr, time_len);

  1245	        time_ptr = tmp;
